Q: 3. How large is the expected dataset?A: depends on mode like wikipediat than massive else medium

Q: 4. Which search modes are must-have for v1?A: All three, ranked & merged

Q: 5. How strict is the "local" requirement?A: try to make 100% offline for that we can downlaoid model like sentencetransformation(not llm) and flexiable for we can use the local llm or API optionally

Q: 6. What is the desired output interface?A: all four but at start we can create full stack app

Q: 7. What should search results return?A: All of the above

Q: 8. How should results from the 3 search modes be merged/re-ranked?A: we can select whatever we want  No re-ranking needed  2 Simple score-based merge (BM25 + vector)  3 LLM re-ranker (local model)  4 Cross-encoder re-ranker (e.g. ms-marco)

Q: 9. What database for storing metadata & chunk text?A: PostgreSQL (production-grade)

Q: 10. What is your preferred backend language/stack?A: Rust (performance-first)Excellent! Now I have a crystal-clear picture. Let me analyze all the open source projects and design your complete system architecture.Now let me build the full architecture document.

Here's your full project blueprint — every layer is clickable to drill deeper. Let me break down each section clearly.

Project name: MemorySearch — local-first semantic search engine

What we learned from the open source projectsLlamaIndex taught us the best chunking strategies: sentence-aware splitting, token-window overlap, and code-aware AST chunking. We mimic its SimpleNodeParser but in Rust.FAISS gave us the ANN (approximate nearest neighbor) playbook: HNSW graph index for high-recall vector search in milliseconds, even at millions of vectors. We use pgvector's HNSW (which wraps FAISS ideas) or FAISS directly via FFI.AnythingLLM showed us how to run all 3 search arms in parallel and merge them — it's the reference for how a local RAG app handles multi-modal retrieval. We replicate its retrieval core but make it mode-aware.Typesense gave us the gold standard for BM25 + fuzzy in one engine. We mimic it using Tantivy (pure Rust, same Lucene-inspired BM25) plus trigram indexes for typo tolerance — 100% offline, no server needed.OpenWebUI showed us how to expose re-ranker selection as a user setting — we borrow that UX pattern directly.

The 3 search arms — how each worksArm 1 — Exact keyword (BM25 via Tantivy). Every chunk is indexed as a Lucene-style inverted index. Query hits are scored by TF-IDF weighted term frequency. Fast, deterministic, no GPU needed.Arm 2 — Fuzzy match (trigram + SymSpell). Each chunk is broken into character 3-grams ("hello" → hel, ell, llo). A query like "resurch" still finds "research" because 2 of 3 trigrams overlap. SymSpell gives sub-millisecond edit-distance correction.Arm 3 — Semantic intent (all-MiniLM + HNSW). Every chunk is embedded into a 384-dim vector using sentence-transformers/all-MiniLM-L6-v2 (downloaded once, ~80MB, fully offline). Queries are embedded at runtime and matched via HNSW cosine similarity — finds results with zero keyword overlap.

Re-ranker modes (selectable per query)The 3 arms each return top-K results with raw scores. The merger picks one strategy:RRF (Reciprocal Rank Fusion) — the default fast path. Scores each doc as Σ 1/(k + rank_i) across arms. No model needed, ~1ms.Cross-encoder (ms-marco-MiniLM) — re-scores every candidate pair (query, chunk) through a small transformer. Best quality, ~50–200ms per query.LLM re-ranker — sends top-20 chunks to a local Ollama model with a "rank these by relevance" prompt. Most intelligent but slowest (~2–5s).

Tech stack summaryLayerTechnologyCore engineRust (Axum web server, Tokio async)Full-text searchTantivy (BM25, Rust-native)Vector indexpgvector HNSW or FAISS via FFIMetadata storePostgreSQLEmbeddingsall-MiniLM-L6-v2 via fastembed-rsFuzzySymSpell-rs + trigram indexPython bridgePyO3 (Rust → Python bindings)Web UIReact + FastAPI (v1 target)Local LLMOllama (llama3, mistral, etc.)Optional cloudAnthropic / OpenAI API

Suggested build order (phases)Phase 1 — Core engine. Rust crate with chunker, embedder, Tantivy BM25, pgvector store, and RRF merge. CLI only. Test with a notes dataset.Phase 2 — Fuzzy + semantic arms. Add SymSpell fuzzy arm and HNSW vector arm. All 3 arms running in parallel via Tokio.Phase 3 — Re-rankers. Add cross-encoder (ms-marco) as default quality mode, Ollama LLM ranker as premium mode.Phase 4 — Full-stack web UI. FastAPI wrapping the Rust core (via PyO3 or HTTP), React frontend with search bar, result cards showing chunk + metadata + LLM answer.Phase 5 — Modes. Wikipedia dump ingestion (streaming XML parser), codebase mode (AST-aware chunking via tree-sitter), Notes mode (Markdown/Obsidian aware).

Want me to start building Phase 1 — the Rust project scaffolding with the chunker, Tantivy BM25 index, and CLI? Or would you like the React UI design first?

Full open-source analysis — what exactly to steal from LlamaIndex, FAISS, AnythingLLM, Typesense, and OpenWebUI, with side-by-side code comparisonsComplete Rust workspace structure with every crate, file, and module laid outAll 3 search arms with actual Rust code — BM25 (Tantivy), fuzzy (SymSpell + trigrams), semantic (pgvector HNSW)All 4 re-ranker modes with implementation — RRF formula, cross-encoder ONNX, LLM re-ranker prompt patternFull PostgreSQL schema with pgvector HNSW index setupMode-aware config (notes.toml, codebase.toml, wikipedia.toml)Chunker implementations — sentence chunker with overlap, AST-aware code chunker via tree-sitterREST API spec with full request/response shapes including latency_ms breakdown per armModel download scripts — all-MiniLM-L6-v2, ms-marco cross-encoder, SymSpell dictionaryPerformance targets per mode with RAM footprint tablePhased roadmap so you can build incrementally and have something working at each phase

✦ I have drafted the master plan covering all 5 phases of the MemorySearch implementation. 

  Please review the detailed plan below. Once you confirm it looks good, I will formally submit it for approval.

  MemorySearch Implementation Plan

  > For agentic workers: REQUIRED SUB-SKILL: Use superpowers:subagent-driven-development or superpowers:executing-plans to implement this plan. This is a high-level master plan covering all 5 phases. Each
  phase may require its own detailed sub-plan during execution.

  Goal: Build a local-first, offline-capable multi-modal semantic search engine in Rust with a React + FastAPI web UI, mimicking Google's search capabilities on local data.

  Architecture: A Rust core engine with Tokio (async), Axum (API), Tantivy (BM25), pgvector (HNSW), and FastEmbed. Three parallel search arms (Exact, Fuzzy, Semantic) merged and re-ranked. Optional RAG
  layer via local Ollama.

  Tech Stack: Rust, Tokio, Axum, PostgreSQL, pgvector, Tantivy, FastEmbed, ONNX Runtime, Python, FastAPI, React, TypeScript, Ollama.

  Global Constraints
   - 100% offline by default (models downloaded locally).
   - Sub-10ms search target for medium datasets.
   - Rust 2021 edition.
   - PostgreSQL 16+ with pgvector extension required.

  ---

  Background & Motivation
  The user requires a multi-modal local search engine that operates entirely offline on personal data (notes, code, Wikipedia). Existing solutions are either cloud-dependent, lack a unified multi-arm
  search (BM25 + Semantic + Fuzzy), or are not optimized for desktop performance. MemorySearch bridges this gap by combining the best features of LlamaIndex, FAISS, AnythingLLM, and Typesense into a
  unified, high-performance Rust binary.

  Scope & Impact
  This master plan covers the full 5-phase roadmap outlined in the architecture document. 
   - Impact: Delivers a fully functional CLI and API backend, followed by a complete web UI and advanced data mode ingestion.
   - Scope: Includes scaffolding the Rust workspace, building the 3 parallel search arms, implementing multiple re-rankers, creating the web UI, and establishing the Python bindings.

  Proposed Solution
  We will implement the architecture in 5 distinct phases, utilizing a modular Cargo workspace (ms-core, ms-ingest, ms-index, ms-search, ms-rerank, ms-rag, ms-server, ms-cli). Each phase adds a discrete
  layer of functionality, starting from a pure text search baseline and culminating in a rich, multi-modal web experience.

  Alternatives Considered
   - Pure Python Backend: Rejected due to performance and memory constraints compared to Rust.
   - Elasticsearch/OpenSearch: Rejected in favor of embedded Tantivy to reduce system dependencies and footprint.
   - Cloud LLM Embeddings (OpenAI): Rejected as the primary method to maintain the strict 100% offline requirement, though cloud APIs will be supported optionally.

  ---

  Phased Implementation Plan

  Phase 1: Setup & Core Engine
  Goal: Establish the Rust workspace, database schema, and BM25 text search via Tantivy.

   - [ ] Step 1: Workspace Scaffolding
     - Initialize the Cargo workspace and create all crates (ms-core, ms-ingest, ms-index, ms-search, ms-rerank, ms-rag, ms-server, ms-cli).
     - Add workspace dependencies (Tokio, Serde, SQLx, Tantivy, etc.).
   - [ ] Step 2: Database Initialization
     - Write SQL migration scripts to enable vector and create documents and chunks tables.
   - [ ] Step 3: Ingestion Pipeline (Text)
     - Implement SentenceChunker in ms-ingest.
     - Implement Tantivy indexing logic in ms-index.
   - [ ] Step 4: Search & CLI
     - Implement BM25 search arm in ms-search.
     - Build the basic ms-cli to ingest directories and search the Tantivy index.

  Phase 2: Fuzzy & Semantic Search Arms
  Goal: Run all 3 search arms in parallel and merge results.

   - [ ] Step 1: Semantic Embedding
     - Integrate fastembed-rs in ms-ingest to generate vectors using all-MiniLM-L6-v2.
     - Store vectors in pgvector during ingestion.
   - [ ] Step 2: Semantic Search Arm
     - Implement vector similarity search query in ms-search against pgvector.
   - [ ] Step 3: Fuzzy Search Arm
     - Integrate symspell-rs and trigram logic in ms-index and ms-search.
   - [ ] Step 4: Query Router & RRF Merge
     - Implement tokio::join! to run all 3 arms concurrently.
     - Implement the RRF (Reciprocal Rank Fusion) algorithm to merge scores.

  Phase 3: Re-rankers & RAG Layer
  Goal: Add high-quality re-ranking and optional LLM answers.

   - [ ] Step 1: Cross-Encoder Re-ranker
     - Integrate ort (ONNX Runtime) in ms-rerank to run ms-marco-MiniLM-L6-v2.
   - [ ] Step 2: RAG Layer
     - Implement LLMProvider trait in ms-rag with support for local Ollama.
     - Implement prompt assembly and answer generation.

  Phase 4: Full-Stack Web UI
  Goal: Expose the engine via API and build the React frontend.

   - [ ] Step 1: REST API (Rust/Axum & Python/FastAPI)
     - Expose /api/search and /api/ingest routes via Axum.
     - Setup the FastAPI bridge.
   - [ ] Step 2: React UI
     - Scaffold Vite/React/TypeScript frontend in ui/.
     - Build SearchBar, ResultCard, and configurations panels.

  Phase 5: Advanced Data Modes & Python Lib
  Goal: Support specialized ingestion and provide a Python SDK.

   - [ ] Step 1: Advanced Loaders
     - Implement streaming Wikipedia XML parser in ms-ingest.
     - Implement AST-aware code chunking using tree-sitter.
   - [ ] Step 2: Python Bindings
     - Use PyO3 in the python/ directory to expose the Rust engine as a Python package.

  ---

  Verification & Testing
   - Unit Tests: Each crate must have unit tests covering core logic (e.g., chunking boundaries, BM25 score calculations, RRF sorting).
   - Integration Tests: End-to-end tests from document ingestion to multi-arm search retrieval.
   - Performance Benchmarks: Verify sub-10ms latency for basic search on 10k chunks and validate memory footprint against targets.

  Migration & Rollback
   - Database schema changes will be managed via sqlx migrations, allowing for structured rollbacks.
   - Index corruption (Tantivy/FAISS) can be resolved by providing a CLI command to wipe and re-index a specific mode from the source documents.

  Does this implementation plan meet your expectations?

  Accomplishments:
   1. Rust Workspace Scaffolding: Initialized a Rust 2021 workspace with 8 core crates (ms-core, ms-ingest, ms-index, ms-search, ms-rerank, ms-rag, ms-server, ms-cli).

   5. Project Knowledge: Updated PROJECT.md with key technical decisions and Phase 1 deliverables.

  Current Status:
   - Tantivy Indexing: Working.
   - CLI Search: Working (BM25 only).
   - Tests: All 7 tests passing (Scaffold validation, Chunker logic, Indexing logic).

✦ Task 5 (Infrastructure & Docker Setup) is complete and committed.

  Key Changes:
   - Simplified Dockerfile: Replaced the manual COPY list of every Cargo.toml with a cleaner COPY . . approach. I've added a .dockerignore file to ensure only necessary source files are sent to the Docker
     daemon, making the build process much easier to maintain as you add new crates.
   - Docker Compose: Committed the docker-compose.yml with profiles for dev (source mounting, cargo caching) and prod (optimized binary).
   - Setup & Infrastructure:
       - Added SETUP_GUIDE.md for both Docker and manual local installation.
       - Added .env.example for environment variable management.
       - Added scripts/download_models.sh to handle offline model retrieval.
   - Project Tracking: Updated PROJECT.md and progress.md to reflect the new infrastructure.

  The project is now fully containerized and ready for collaborative development.

  Would you like to continue with Phase 2 (Fuzzy & Semantic Search Arms) now?
